Do NOT synthesize yourself.\n5. **Output**: Follow the output instructions exactly as specified in your task instruction.\n\n\n# Task: Express Security + Reliability + Compatibility Hardening Sweep\n\n## Background\n\nYou are a Node.js platform engineer responsible for a comprehensive hardening sweep on an Express 4.x fork used by multiple internal services.\n\nThe baseline branch has three critical security and reliability issues:\n\n1. **HTTP Header Injection (CRLF)** â€” The response and request pipelines lack explicit CRLF validation. Request-side trust boundaries do not sanitize tainted headers. Response-side APIs do not reject header names/values with `\\r` or `\\n` characters. This enables header injection attacks across cookies, redirects, and custom headers. **This is the primary security concern.**\n2. **Async Error Propagation** â€” Rejected promises from handlers are not consistently forwarded to error middleware. A handler that calls `next(err)` synchronously and also returns a rejected promise can invoke the error handler twice, or the error may be swallowed entirely. This reduces observability and can hide failures in production.\n3. **Node.js 22 Compatibility Cleanup** â€” Legacy APIs and patterns remain in `lib/request.js` (e.g., `this.connection` instead of `this.socket`, `trimRight()` instead of `trimEnd()`). While functionality is preserved, modern Node.js versions deprecate these patterns.\n\nYou need to deliver a single coherent patch that addresses all three classes without breaking existing synchronous behavior.\n\n## Scope\n\nWork in the Express source at `/testbed/lib/`.\n\nPrimary files:\n\n- `lib/utils.js` â€” Shared validation utilities\n- `lib/response.js` â€” Response-side header/cookie/redirect validation\n- `lib/request.js` â€” Request-side trust boundary and compatibility cleanup\n- `lib/router/layer.js` â€” Async error propagation in handler execution\n- `lib/router/index.js` â€” Async error propagation in param pipeline\n\n## Requirements\n\n### A) HTTP Header Injection Hardening (Primary â€” 40% of verifier weight)\n\n1. **Implement a shared CRLF validation utility** in `lib/utils.js`:\n   - Detect both literal `\\r` and `\\n` characters AND escaped sequences `\\\\r` and `\\\\n` in strings\n   - Export as `containsInvalidHeaderChar(value)` â€” return `true` if any CRLF is present\n   - Handle arrays, strings, numbers, booleans, null, undefined gracefully\n\n2. **Response-side hardening** in `lib/response.js`:\n   - Reject CRLF in `res.set()` / `res.header()` for both names and values\n   - Reject CRLF in `res.append()` (used for Set-Cookie and multi-value headers)\n   - Reject CRLF in `res.cookie()` for cookie names and values\n   - Reject CRLF in `res.location()` / `res.redirect()` for the target URL\n   - Throw a `TypeError` or similar error for any CRLF-tainted input before reaching the native `setHeader` call. Valid inputs must pass through unchanged.\n\n3. **Request-side hardening** in `lib/request.js`:\n   - Sanitize `req.get()` and `req.header()` to return `undefined` for CRLF-tainted header values\n   - Sanitize `req.referer` / `req.referrer` property to return `undefined` for CRLF-tainted values\n   - **Critical trust boundary:** When computing `req.hostname`, reject any CRLF in the trusted `X-Forwarded-Host` header\n   - Do not fall through to the `Host` header if `X-Forwarded-Host` contains CRLF â€” return `undefined`\n\n### B) Async Error Handling (Secondary â€” 35% of verifier weight)\n\n4. Async route/middleware errors must propagate to Express error handlers.\n5. If a handler calls `next(err)` synchronously and the returned promise later rejects, error handling must run once only (called-once guard).\n6. `next('route')` / `next('router')` behavior must remain correct.\n7. Async `app.param()` handlers in `router/index.js` must be handled (they bypass `layer.handle_request`).\n\n### C) Node.js 22 Compatibility Cleanup (Tertiary â€” 15% of verifier weight)\n\n8. Replace deprecated/legacy request internals in `lib/request.js`:\n   - use `this.socket` instead of `this.connection`\n   - replace `trimRight()` with `trimEnd()`\n9. Preserve behavior while removing those legacy usages.\n\n### General Constraints\n\n10. Keep synchronous behavior unchanged where not explicitly part of this task.\n11. Do not add new dependencies.\n12. Modify only files under `lib/`.\n13. All CRLF validation must use the shared utility from `lib/utils.js` â€” consistency is required for correctness.\n\n## Deliverable\n\nA patch that satisfies all verifier checks for CRLF injection prevention (primary), async error propagation (secondary), and Node 22 compatibility (tertiary).\n\n## Acceptance Criteria\n\n- Verifier passes all 43 tests (32 runtime + 11 static checks).\n- CRLF validation is implemented via shared utility exported from `lib/utils.js`.\n- Both request and response paths use the same utility consistently.\n- No legacy `this.connection` / `trimRight()` usage remains in `lib/request.js`.\n- All CRLF entry points (res.set, res.append, res.cookie, res.location, req.get, req.header, req.referer, req.hostname) are hardened.\n- Async error propagation works correctly for nested routers, array handlers, param callbacks, and mixed sync/async middleware.\n\n\n## Gold Decomposition Guide\ntask_id: express-async-errors\npattern: fan-out-synthesize\ndescription: >\n  Express 4.x comprehensive hardening sweep with primary focus on CRLF injection\n  prevention across request/response pipelines, supported by async error propagation\n  reliability and Node.js 22 compatibility cleanup. Three concurrent workstreams\n  with deep specialization: CRLF security, async reliability, and compatibility.\n\nagents:\n  - id: agent-crlf-utils\n    assignment: Design and implement the shared CRLF validation utility\n    context_budget: small\n    description: |\n      Own lib/utils.js.\n      Deliver: A reusable exports.containsInvalidHeaderChar function that detects\n      both literal CR/LF characters and escaped sequences (\\r, \\n) in any value type.\n      The utility must be robust to arrays, nulls, booleans, and numbers.\n      This utility becomes the single source of truth for CRLF validation across\n      both request and response paths. Export it clearly so other modules can import it.\n\n  - id: agent-crlf-response\n    assignment: Harden all response-side header/cookie/redirect entry points\n    context_budget: medium\n    description: |\n      Own lib/response.js.\n      Deliver: Import the shared CRLF utility and wire it into every response API\n      that sets headers: res.set(), res.append(), res.cookie(), res.location(), res.redirect().\n      Any attempt to set a header (name or value), cookie (name or value), or redirect URL\n      that contains CRLF must be rejected with a TypeError before reaching the native\n      setHeader call. Valid inputs must pass through unchanged.\n      This agent ensures the response pipeline is locked down against header injection.\n\n  - id: agent-crlf-request\n    assignment: Harden request-side trust boundaries and header access\n    context_budget: medium\n    description: |\n      Own lib/request.js.\n      Deliver: Import the shared CRLF utility and sanitize all request header access\n      methods (req.get(), req.header(), req.referer). Any read of a CRLF-tainted header\n      value must return undefined, not the tainted value. Additionally, enforce the critical\n      trust boundary in req.hostname: when X-Forwarded-Host is trusted but contains CRLF,\n      reject it immediately â€” do not fall through to the Host header. This prevents\n      a trusted-but-tainted header from bypassing the security check and compromising hostname resolution.\n\n  - id: agent-async-errors\n    assignment: Fix async error propagation in routing and param handling\n    context_budget: medium\n    description: |\n      Own lib/router/layer.js and lib/router/index.js.\n      Deliver: Both layer.js handle_request() and handle_error() must detect when a handler\n      returns a Promise and attach appropriate error handlers. A called-once guard prevents\n      double-invocation if the handler both calls next(err) synchronously and returns a rejected\n      promise. Similarly, the param pipeline in router/index.js must wrap app.param() callbacks\n      with the same guard, as those bypass the normal layer.handle_request flow.\n      Ensure async handlers throw, async middleware throw, and async param callbacks all\n      propagate errors to the error handler exactly once.\n\n  - id: agent-compat-request\n    assignment: Modernize request internals for Node.js 22\n    context_budget: small\n    description: |\n      Own lib/request.js (in conjunction with agent-crlf-request for CRLF work).\n      Deliver: Replace deprecated request internals throughout lib/request.js:\n      this.connection -> this.socket, trimRight() -> trimEnd().\n      Preserve all existing behavior while removing legacy patterns.\n      This work is independent of CRLF hardening but shares the same file;\n      ensure CRLF and compat changes do not conflict.\n\n  - id: agent-orchestrator\n    assignment: Integrate all workstreams, validate consistency, pass full test suite\n    context_budget: large\n    depends_on: [agent-crlf-utils, agent-crlf-response, agent-crlf-request, agent-async-errors, agent-compat-request]\n    description: |\n      Receive deliverables from all specialist agents.
